<span id="freeTextContainer16265592432566118193">You just have to love Katherine Rundell: "She begins each day with a cartwheel and believes that reading is almost exactly the same as cartwheeling: it turns the world upside down and leaves you breathless." One year old Sophie is found floating in a cello case, and is adopted by bachelor, Charles Maxim, after they survive a shipwreck. He raises her unconventionally, always encouraging her to consider the possibles. When Sophie turns 12, Social Services decides it is inappropriate for her to liv</span>
  <span id="freeText16265592432566118193" style="display:none">You just have to love Katherine Rundell: "She begins each day with a cartwheel and believes that reading is almost exactly the same as cartwheeling: it turns the world upside down and leaves you breathless." One year old Sophie is found floating in a cello case, and is adopted by bachelor, Charles Maxim, after they survive a shipwreck. He raises her unconventionally, always encouraging her to consider the possibles. When Sophie turns 12, Social Services decides it is inappropriate for her to live with Charles, and they flee together to Paris to search for Sophie's mother, who Sophie believes is alive. In Paris, Sophie is befriended by Matteo and others, who live on the rooftops, away from the prying eyes of society. Their adventures are fun and magical. Also liked that Rundell used the names of animal groups liberally, such as a murder of crows, a murmuration of starlings, a knot of toads, etc.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2172231944" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3722477698265324337">Some imperfections in the details, but it has an interesting adventure, delightful characters, some very lovely writing, and besides, it's so very original & creative that it gets the bonus star. Read an edition with a dark cover, like the one I did... the current GR default is *wrong* because rooftoppers do *not* want to be seen and so are mostly nocturnal. And do read it; it's short and gives one hope that there will continue to be *new* stories in the world.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1993485522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13605962638167855890">Pick your suit: reading this book in a balcony with morning summer air and lime and birds chirping OR reading this book by the window in rainy night accompanied by hot chocolate and your cat. Either way, this book will give you a dazzling, dreamy sense of adventure.<br/><br/>This books fill my heart with so much feels and warmth. I can't help but thinking about Heidi and Amélie (yes, Audrey Totou). Even though the pace needs some time to pick up and the ending is too rushed for my liking, this book is so </span>
  <span id="freeText13605962638167855890" style="display:none">Pick your suit: reading this book in a balcony with morning summer air and lime and birds chirping OR reading this book by the window in rainy night accompanied by hot chocolate and your cat. Either way, this book will give you a dazzling, dreamy sense of adventure.<br /><br />This books fill my heart with so much feels and warmth. I can't help but thinking about Heidi and Amélie (yes, Audrey Totou). Even though the pace needs some time to pick up and the ending is too rushed for my liking, this book is so dreamy and easy to swallow. I like how the author picked a very unique perspective of the rooftoppers: eating pigeons and diving to collect wishing-coins to live.<br /><br />I don't know what else to say. This is the kind of book that just... stays.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/627875124" />
    <a title="jesse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1185127-jesse"><img alt="jesse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532961676p2/1185127.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/627875124?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jesse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jesse" href="/user/show/1185127-jesse">jesse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/21378592-rooftoppers">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to jesse by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer627875124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4212161819978582759"><a href='http://grouchyrobot.files.wordpress.com/2014/03/rooftoppers_v2.png' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img alt='rooftoppers_v2' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394045850i/8800437.png' width='450' height='225' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>magical things can happen on rooftops – or at least should.<br/><br/>when i was still at an age and height where i couldn't reach the cupboard's highest and thus of course most mysterious shelf --even when stretching and standing on tiptoes (there may have been frustrated grunting involved), my family and i would fly over to my grandparents in india during our summer holidays.<br/><br/>we kids were bored out of our minds.<br/><br/>without further ado we'd decide that it was an amazingly ingenious idea to jump from roofto</span>
  <span id="freeText4212161819978582759" style="display:none"><a href="http://grouchyrobot.files.wordpress.com/2014/03/rooftoppers_v2.png" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="rooftoppers_v2" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394045850i/8800437.png" width="450" height="225" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>magical things can happen on rooftops – or at least should.<br><br>when i was still at an age and height where i couldn't reach the cupboard's highest and thus of course most mysterious shelf --even when stretching and standing on tiptoes (there may have been frustrated grunting involved), my family and i would fly over to my grandparents in india during our summer holidays.<br><br>we kids were bored out of our minds.<br><br>without further ado we'd decide that it was an amazingly ingenious idea to jump from rooftop to rooftop and explore other people's properties where we would, among other things, pet stray cats, feed impatiently clucking chickens, see the birth of puppies, go --what can be best described as—‘people-watching’ and shoot spitballs at innocent civilians. on the downside, we managed to damage our neighbor’s already somewhat leaky rooftop and our parents were furious when they found out what we've done. of course we wouldn't let that stop us,- instead we were just more careful about it.<br><br>something that <i>rundell</i> easily manages is capturing how as a child you somehow always strive to have your own adventure; that is if it doesn't find its way to you beforehand. a small thing that may seem trivial to an adult could be invaluable to a child. <i>rooftoppers</i> keeps reminding the reader that beautiful things can happen particularly in childhood when you're not yet set in your ways, keep an open mind accept people and things the way they are in their varying shapes and forms. children don't give a damn about customs, manners and danger. stupid mistakes are bound to happen of course, but it's kind of sad how we develop this aversion to taking risks based on the experience we have made, instead of showing more courage like we did when we were children.<br><br>if you have ever seen and enjoyed <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0211915/?ref_=nv_sr_1" rel="nofollow noopener">amélie</a> [<a href="http://youtu.be/B-uxeZaM-VM" rel="nofollow noopener">trailer</a>], <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0364517/?ref_=nv_sr_1" rel="nofollow noopener">love me if you dare</a> [<a href="http://youtu.be/ICaicXbuNSU" rel="nofollow noopener">trailer</a>] or any <a href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm0027572/?ref_=nv_sr_1" rel="nofollow noopener">wes anderson film</a>, then you have a small taste of what you can expect from <i>rooftoppers</i>. if you haven't ... even better: dive into it with closed eyes and be prepared to have your inner child’s mind blown with this whimsical little tale. i wish i could give this to my 7 year old self that would cherish this and probably leave a bigger impression than on my by now adult version. it's the stuff that childhood dreams are made of, encouraging children to believe, if only for a little while longer.<br><br><b>quotes:</b><br><blockquote>"she will come," she said. “or i'll go to her."<br><br>"no, sophie. that is not how the world works." miss eliot was sure that sophie was mistaken, but then miss eliot was also sure that cross-stitch was <i>vital</i>, and charles was <i>impossible</i>, which just showed that adults weren't always right.<br><br>one day sophie found some red paint and wrote the name of the ship, the <i>queen mary</i>, and the date of the storm on the white wall of the house, just in case her mother passed by.<br><br>charles's face, when he found her, was too complicated for her to look at. but he helped her reach the high parts and wash the brushes afterward.<br><br>"a case", he said to miss eliot, "of the just in cases."<br><br>"but she's-"<br><br>"she is only doing as i have told her."<br><br>"you told her to vandalize your own house?"<br><br>"no. i have told her not to ignore life's possibles."<br><br>[6%]<br><br>-.-.-.-.-.-.-.-.-.-.-.-.<br><br>"is the girl worth it? worth committing a felony?"<br><br>"she is," said charles evenly.<br><br>"she is bright enough to start a forest fire."<br><br>"she seemed fairly ordinary," said the clerk. crouched outside, sophie bristled.<br><br>"people usually do, until you know them," said charles.<br><br>"sophie is uniquely endowed with intelligence, grit, and, at this particular moment, coffee stains. in fact, speaking of which-" a chair scraped, and sophie just had time to stumble backward two steps before the door opened.<br><br>[35%]</blockquote><br><b>book pairing:</b><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7952209-the-kneebone-boy?ac=1" rel="nofollow noopener">the kneebone boy</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4212161819978582759" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <i>Mothers are worth hunting for.</i>

Things are fine for years, but then <i>The Authorities</i> catch wind of the arrangement . . . and, of course, they get involved.<br/><br/>Sophie and Charles head for Paris, both to avoid the child services' busybodies, and to look for Sophie's mother.   <span id="freeText13891894397144877423" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Mothers are worth hunting for.</i>
</b><br><br>Charles is a happy bachelor when he finds a baby floating in a cello case in the English Channel. He names her Sophie, and takes her home to raise. Things are fine for years, but then <i>The Authorities</i> catch wind of the arrangement . . . and, of course, they get involved.<br><br>Sophie and Charles head for Paris, both to avoid the child services' busybodies, and to look for Sophie's mother. There Sophie's fondness for hanging about on rooftops allows her to meet a whole new group of Parisians, and to see sights few others get to view.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500319170i/23323105._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And, best of all - the rooftops just might lead to her mother.<br><br>Rundell's story is beautifully written, and involving. Parts were a bit far-fetched, but on the whole, it is a marvelous read, and highly recommended. <br><br>I listened to the audio book, which features a wonderful performance by Nicola Barber.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17480756247702862322">Woah, I can't believe that is the cover they show you! The one I've got is so beautiful... Anyway I guess I should start talking about the book? Well to start let me just say I have not read anything that has been so completely and shockingly beautiful that I am way past crying in about... well a long time. I think it may have been aimed at younger audiences but it mattered not. The story was so utterly simple but wonderful in this simplicity. You fell in love with all of the characters despite </span>
  <span id="freeText17480756247702862322" style="display:none">Woah, I can't believe that is the cover they show you! The one I've got is so beautiful... Anyway I guess I should start talking about the book? Well to start let me just say I have not read anything that has been so completely and shockingly beautiful that I am way past crying in about... well a long time. I think it may have been aimed at younger audiences but it mattered not. The story was so utterly simple but wonderful in this simplicity. You fell in love with all of the characters despite their imperfection. Katherine Rundell was able to portray a complete picture of characters with the merest of words. Every aspect of this story I loved. I would wonder when it was set but I really don't care for once. I don't care about the history or the facts, all I cared about was the way I cried at the very last page. Both because of the ending itself and the fat that the book was finished. I will be getting more of Katherine's book promptly. </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer755788019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1581775350023487339">Utterly gorgeous from start to finish, this has all the charm and security of a Noel Streatfield novel with a lovely, fresh twist to the writing that makes it a joy to read. It has a slightly strange structure, and I was hoping for something a bit more rounded from the ending, but all in all this is absolutely wonderful, an instant children's classic.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oPOlStCXkHHQRBUigDoAjnK/5IM8/joPAK/7vr6My5kH983lG0n1jC1C/YZivLO8ldKMVbvAC1klg+PM1PnvwQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WTIMbuPRkcW07jtRWng70tVACkaIS/f8hBK2KmuSFyn+NmTBKA/0OEno0/W4/ojgMi1ikA91xqqhPq5YAeczcQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7062634026651995126">Katherine Rundell was born in 1987 and grew up in Africa and Europe. In 2008 she was elected a Fellow of All Souls College, Oxford. Her first book, The Girl Savage, was born of her love of Zimbabwe and her own childhood there; her second, Rooftoppers, was inspired by summers working in Paris and by night-time trespassing on the rooftops of All Souls. She is currently working on her doctorate along</span>
  <span id="freeText7062634026651995126" style="display:none">Katherine Rundell was born in 1987 and grew up in Africa and Europe. In 2008 she was elected a Fellow of All Souls College, Oxford. Her first book, The Girl Savage, was born of her love of Zimbabwe and her own childhood there; her second, Rooftoppers, was inspired by summers working in Paris and by night-time trespassing on the rooftops of All Souls. She is currently working on her doctorate alongside an adult novel.<br /><br />Source: <a href="http://www.faber.co.uk/catalog/author/katherine-rundell#sthash.pEoxU0iL.dpuf" rel="nofollow noopener"> Katherine Rundell</a></span>
